Set standards for county party headquarters to carry out organizational propaganda and people's movement work. (24th Central News Agency Telegram)

Wuhu Rice Market in Dire Straits: Banks Stop Providing Loans to External Warehouses, Market Prices Sluggish and Ignored 69

Wuhu Correspondent: Wuhu is the gathering area for rice and grain from various counties in southern Anhui. At its peak, annual rice exports reached as much as 8 million shi. Therefore, the prosperity and decline of the commercial market in southern Anhui, the economic circulation in rural villages of various counties, and even the financial surplus or deficit of the province are largely dependent on the Wuhu rice market. The largest recipients of Wuhu rice for export are the Guangzhou-Chaozhou and Yantai-Ningbo cartels. However, due to the large scale of business, they heavily rely on credit loans from money shops for turnover. In the past, when finance was active, there were seven or eight mechanized rice mills and seventy or eighty traditional rice husking workshops involved in the rice business. There were even more firms involved in purchasing, transporting, and exporting rice. The money shops provided credit loans, with turnovers constantly fluctuating around one million yuan, with no less than several hundred thousand yuan at the lowest. Every time new grain was harvested, rice boats lined the riverbank with masts resembling a forest. However, after the great flood of the 20th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1931], the rural economy collapsed, and commerce declined in tandem. The money shops, being affected and unable to support themselves, closed down one after another. To date, only five remain, barely hanging on. The rice mills and husking workshops are still able to obtain loans from the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, and Industrial Bank by pledging goods. They rely on these loans for turnover to barely stay afloat. Unexpectedly, in the past two years, the Bank of China and Bank of Communications have also been affected by fraud by the factory owners, incurring considerable losses. They have become wary of pledging loans against this type of collateral. In addition, the dumping of foreign rice has invisibly blocked the Guangzhou-Chaozhou and Yantai-Ningbo markets. The rice market has fallen into a state of complete stagnation, and all industries are in a state of dire collapse. Although this year has again seen uneven disasters of flood and drought, the harvests in various counties of southern Anhui are still extremely abundant. However, recently, both the Bank of China and Bank of Communications in Wuhu received orders from their Shanghai headquarters that, because the Criminal Code has already been changed (Article 337 of the old Criminal Code: "Illegally taking leased property constitutes theft"; Article 339: "Property owned by oneself but pledged as collateral is considered the property of others") (The clauses in the new Criminal Code that treat property owned by oneself but pledged as collateral as the property of others have been deleted; compensation can only be sought under the Civil Code), therefore, they will immediately stop providing collateralized loans to external warehouses due to the lack of legal protection, and order them to expand internal warehouses. This has made it difficult for factories with a shortage of capital to operate. Even the Guangzhou-Chaozhou cartels, which have always relied on credit, have been limited to a maximum credit loan of only 5,000 yuan per household by the silver and money industries, and they must repay the previous loan before another can be granted, making it impossible to collect and transport goods freely. With such restrictions on finance, it is feared that there is no way to salvage the rice market, which is on the verge of collapse. Currently, new rice is entering the market in increasing quantities. Although high-grade machine-milled rice has softened to 7.12 yuan, and medium-grade polished rice is at 6.67 yuan, the cartels can only stand by and watch. The Wuhu Chamber of Commerce believes that if this continues, the rice market will have no hope of recovery, and there is a danger that it will automatically shift downstream. This would bring the commerce of Wuhu and the finances of various counties to the brink of collapse. Therefore, it is preparing to request the authorities to find ways to provide relief in order to avert the crisis. (August 23rd)

Extreme Shortage of Cash in Newly Recovered Areas of Southern Jiangxi: Provincial Government Borrows One Million Yuan to Purchase New Grain 70

Nanchang Correspondent: This province suffered a drought disaster last year, but the bandit areas of southern Jiangxi had a relatively abundant harvest. This year's flood disaster did not affect Ganxian and the counties bordering western Jiangxi. Therefore, all the fields in the newly recovered areas that have been restored to cultivation have been celebrating a bumper harvest. However, the above-mentioned areas are all remote areas with obstructed transportation. Before the bandits occupied the area, there were very few outlets for all agricultural products, except for self-sufficiency. After seven or eight years of banditry, cash is extremely scarce, and outside merchants are hesitant to enter the area. Local small merchants lack the capital to operate. As a result, no one is interested in the abundant grain. However, after suffering from disasters, the farmers have nothing, and they hope to exchange grain for cash to meet their urgent needs. Even the rural society relies entirely on the sale of grain and agricultural products as the driving force for circulation. Therefore, farmers have no choice but to sell the grain they obtained with their blood and sweat at a reduced price. In Ji'an, Ganzhou, Xinfeng and other places with access to rivers, each dan of grain costs less than 3 yuan. In places without access to rivers, it is only around 2 yuan. In Guangchang, Lingdu, Taihe, and other bandit areas that have been recovered recently, the price of grain is as low as 1 yuan per dan. Cheap grain hurts farmers, and abundant harvests become a disaster. This is an extreme contradiction compared to the disaster areas of northern Jiangxi, where grain is extremely scarce and the price of rice is still around 10 yuan. The provincial government has approved at a provincial affairs meeting to borrow 1 million yuan from Yumin Bank, Municipal Bank, Central Bank, Chinese Bank, and Farmers Bank to purchase new grain in newly recovered areas, including Linghui, Ruizhi, Guangchang, Wanan, and Taihe. It will also handle storage, collateral, transportation, and sales. This is tantamount to providing cash to the disaster victims in the recovered areas. After the purchase, the locations and prices for the sale of the grain will be designated through unified management before transportation is initiated to provide relief and regulate circulation in areas severely affected by flooding, such as Jiujiang, Xingzi, Yongxiu, Hukou, and De'an.

Fujian Province Improves Agriculture and Forestry; Provincial Government Implements Various Plans 71

Fuzhou Correspondent: The Fujian Provincial Government has recently been making efforts in agriculture and forestry. The following is a record of the various ongoing projects:

(A) Establishing Agricultural and Forestry Experiment Stations: Four have already been established: (1) Changle Agricultural Station: Changle is a rice-growing area. The mission of this agricultural station is to conduct research and experiments on improving rice, as well as studying animal husbandry. The plan is to grow rice twice a year and wheat once, to achieve three harvests a year. (2) Nanping Forestry Station: Nanping is an area for afforestation. Currently, 100 mu of barren hills have been designated in the Wangtai area, which is sufficient for afforestation for the time being. (3) Fu'an Tea Station: Eastern Fujian is famous for its tea production. The station plans to use scientific methods to provide practical guidance to farmers on cultivation, so that it will become the central mechanism for improving the tea industry. (4) Zhangpu Agricultural Station: Southern Fujian is known for its fruits, such as sugarcane, bananas, oranges, and lychees. Therefore, the station focuses on horticultural experiments. There are also Longyan Agricultural Station being prepared, which focuses on the improvement of tobacco and cotton. Personnel have been sent there to make plans.

(B) Organizing a Forestry Silver Survey Team: It is jointly composed of specialized members of the Ministry of Industries, forestry professors of Jinling University, and technicians from the Department of Construction. It has already traveled from northern Fujian to western Fujian. According to its investigation report, the natural conditions such as climate and geology in this province are very conducive to afforestation.

(C) Dispatching Personnel to Investigate the Tea Industry: In recent years, the production and sales of tea in this province have declined. To improve and remedy the situation, special personnel have been dispatched to various places in Nanyang and India to investigate planting, manufacturing, and marketing methods for reference. The personnel have now returned to China, and the materials obtained are being organized.

(D) Loan of Soybean Cakes and Sugarcane Seedlings: Xinghua and Zhangzhou are the center of the sugar industry in this province. However, planting and manufacturing have adhered to the old methods and have not been improved, and they are gradually declining. Currently, the Department of Construction is providing loans of sugarcane seedlings and soybean cakes to farmers in Zhangpu and Putian counties in order to promote the improvement of sugarcane. It is also preparing to use 20,000 to 30,000 yuan to improve sugarcane seedlings, which will be distributed to farmers next spring.

(E) Conscripting Labor for Afforestation: It is planned to conscript a large number of laborers in Gutian, Minqing, and other counties along the Min River. The government will provide money, and the people will provide labor to cooperate in building large-scale public forests.

(F) Improving Seasonal Fruits: The oranges of Fuzhou and the tangerines of Zhangzhou are famous throughout the country, but they are all produced in winter and cannot be stored until summer. Currently, storage methods are being studied. Lychees and longans are also famous special products of this province, but they cannot be produced in large quantities due to pest damage. Currently, pest control methods are being studied, and considerable results have been seen. The method is not very difficult.

(G) Training Personnel: In addition to sponsoring Fujian College to open an agricultural department, agricultural schools have been added in Fu'an, Changle, Nanping, and other places. Students are also being sent to study at the agricultural departments of Central University and Jinling University. Agricultural specialists are recruited and employed. (August 21st)

Planning the Guangdong-Guangxi Railway: Extending the Guangzhou-Sanshui Railway to He County; Second Route Survey Begins 72

Guangzhou Correspondent: The Guangdong and Guangxi authorities previously proposed to develop southwest transportation by extending the existing Guangzhou-Sanshui Railway from Hekou Station in Sanshui, Guangdong, through Sihui and Guangning to He County in Guangxi, a length of approximately 230 kilometers. The estimated construction cost is 10 million yuan in national currency. Once the railway tracks are laid, 75 freight cars, 18 passenger cars with 50 seats, and 9 locomotives of 54 tons will be purchased, requiring a total of over 13 million yuan. The project is scheduled to be completed in two years. This plan has been approved by the Ministry of Railways. In the previous year, the Southern Section Administration of the Guangdong-Han Railway dispatched technicians to join Yang Cong, a staff officer of the Guangxi Military Department, and surveying personnel to survey the extension route. The results of the initial survey were submitted to the Ministry of Railways for record, and at the same time, the central government was requested to allocate a portion of the Boxer Indemnity funds to subsidize the construction. The remaining amount would be the responsibility of the two Guangdong governments to raise. Subsequently, the project was shelved due to insufficient funds on both sides. Recently, the authorities have leaned towards construction, and Li Xiangen, Director of the Guangdong-Shaoguan Railway Bureau, went north to propose the Sanhe (i.e., from Sanshui, Guangdong, to He County, Guangxi) Railway construction project to the Nanjing authorities in order to implement the construction. The method of raising funds would be either through the central government allocating funds or by issuing construction bonds. Recently, Li returned to Guangdong, and there have been signs regarding the railway construction. The Guangdong Provincial Government recently ordered the Provincial Department of Construction to cooperate with the Guangzhou-Sanshui Railway Bureau in handling this matter and dispatched Zhuo Kangcheng, the former director of the Zhushao Section Engineering Bureau, to preside over the second survey. After being dispatched, Zhuo visited Zhang Renmin, Chief of Staff of the Guangxi Military Department, to discuss the Guangdong and Guangxi personnel to conduct the survey again. This survey team was organized yesterday and has already started work, starting from the end of the Sanshui Hekou Station of the Guangzhou-Sanshui Railway, and conducting surveys according to the map. It is expected to be completed in one month. Once the review is completed, all preparations will be made to proceed. (August 20th)

Recent Situation of Pacification in Southern Jiangxi: Remnants of Bandits in Youshan and An'yuan are Gradually Eliminated; Second Major Flood in Zhang and Gong Rivers 73

Guangzhou Correspondent: Since the remnants of bandits fled into southern Jiangxi, there are very few remnants left. The First Army of Guangdong, which is currently stationed in the area, has been actively carrying out pacification. According to a recent returnee from southern Jiangxi, the First Army is currently ordering the counties to implement the Baojia system, conduct household registration surveys, and compile company and platoon teams to support local people's self-defense and self-governance. As for the remnants of bandits in various places, the First Army has dispatched teams to search and suppress them to eradicate them completely. Recently, bandit traces were discovered in Youshan and An'yuan and other places. Li Zhen's troops from the First Regiment are still stationed in the Nanxiong to Dayu area to consolidate the area. Currently, the route from Xinfeng to An'yuan is peaceful, and merchants can carry silver and goods back and forth without worry. The authorities are simultaneously carrying out construction. The Xinfeng Bridge has started construction and is expected to be completed in about three months. After the bridge is completed, cars on the Xinfeng Highway can directly reach An'yuan City, making military and civilian transportation more convenient than before. Recently, due to the major floods in the country, Jiangxi Province has not been spared. However, the counties of southern Jiangxi were affected by the first major flood of this year. Unexpectedly, starting on the 8th of this month, the water level of the Zhang and Gong Rivers rose again, flooding the north and south banks. All the bridges along the river from Ganxian to Dayu were destroyed by the flood. The low-lying areas from Ganxian to Nankang, Du Dayu, and Xinfeng became swamps. The disaster area, where transportation was cut off and fields and homes were washed away, left disaster victims everywhere. In addition to telegraphing north and south for relief, the county magistrates of the above counties are purchasing rice with donations from local people to help the victims. The counties have temporarily established a joint flood relief committee to handle disaster relief matters and have telegraphed Gan, Yue, and Shanghai to call for unified donations to save the survivors after the disaster.

Zhenjiang Report: The Jiangsu Provincial Agricultural Management Committee held its first meeting on the 22nd, chaired by Shen Baixian, to discuss the following items: (1) A proposal to allocate large tracts of wasteland by the province to establish provincial-run economic farms to lead agricultural improvement in practice. Rising Water Levels Threaten Northern Tongshan 75

Xuzhou Correspondent: For months, the Yellow River from western Shandong has flooded northern Jiangsu. Feng and Pei have repeatedly reported alarms, but the water in Fengpei is temporarily stable. Since the 17th, the dangerous situation has concentrated in northern Tongshan. The northern border of Fengpei is where the water from Yutai flows in. It relies on the newly built Fengpei Northern Dike as a barrier. This dike is far from the lake, and after several blockages, the water from Yutai has gradually slowed down, and it is temporarily safe. The Lanjia Dam in northern Tongshan is the southern outlet of Weishan Lake. The rising water levels are rushing down. The mouth of the dam has been widened by eight meters after the Special Commissioner accepted the opinion of the Shandong representative. The downstream Jing River does not have enough flow, and the water overflows. The situation is extremely dangerous in the Tongshan area. The following is a record of the on-site inspection:

Tongshan's Northern Water Defense Line 76

Before the Shang Dynasty, Tongshan was the course of the Yellow River, and in the north there was Weishan Lake. After the river shifted, lake transportation was not abandoned. Therefore, from Chengbu to the lakeside, there are three historical water defense lines. The first line is Lanjia Dam, with Shen Dam as the outlet of the lake. The outlet enters the Jing River. The dam starts from Zhanggu Mountain in the west and extends to Mama Mountain in the east, which is enough to restrain the water flow. The second line is the Da Di of Chedao Kou. The area relies on high ground and mountains to form a dike that can extend to the foot of Jiuli Mountain and behind Zifang Mountain. The third line is the former Yellow River's northern dike. Before the river shifted, it was used to internally contain the Yellow River and externally block the microcurrent. However, after the river shifted and transportation was abandoned, the dike was neglected for a long time. All three defense lines have lost their defensive capabilities. Therefore, Tongyi's work to prevent the Yellow River started from the first Lanjia Dam, which was reorganized and cultivated. It was only because the newly built soil was loose and the Jing River had been dredged for a long time that the water resistance was weak and the drainage capacity was insufficient. As a result, the upstream surge caused flooding.

Lake Flooding Situation 77

Tongshan County Magistrate Wang Gongyu, accompanied by Liu Xinyuan, director of the Construction Section, and Zhang Yaxuan, deputy captain of the Security Brigade, have been at the construction site day and night since the construction of the dam began. The (17th) telegram reached Chengbu, stating that the microcurrent was rising and the dikes were in danger. Blue Weibin of the Provincial Party Committee, Dai Zhiqiang of the County Party Committee, and a part of the Party and government staff, as well as representatives of the press, went to inspect by car yesterday morning. They passed through Checunkou, Wanzhai, and arrived at Zhanggu Mountain. Checunkou and Wanzhai are places where the Bulao River and Machang Lake pass through the diversion river. Wanzhai is the mouth of the Bulao River, and Checunkou is the mouth of the Machang Lake River. The water level in the Bulao River, which passes north of Wanzhai, rose sharply by one meter on the 17th, and Wanzhai has been surrounded by water. The water at the mouth of the Checunkou River has been poured into Machang Lake. Machang Lake has been dry for a long time and has now been submerged. Fortunately, the township of Xiaodian was ordered by the First District Office to close the river mouth gate with wooden boards, and the water has not continued to flow in. However, if the water continues to rise, Wanzhai will inevitably be in danger. The car arrived at Zhanggu Mountain, and tens of thousands of civilians were rushing to rescue the disaster. The microcurrent broke through the Jing Mountain People's Dike, seven miles north of the Lanjia Dam, and flooded to the mouth. After the mouth was widened, the flow was extremely violent. The Jing River channel was shallow and could not accommodate it, so it overflowed to the southwest. The civilians urgently built a embankment to block the water, but the water continued to rise, flooding two civilians' embankments and flowing north, attacking the outer layer of the western dike of Weishan Lake. The water inside the dike was three meters deep. The Great Dike was extremely dangerous due to the two-sided turbulence, and the southern end of the dike, about ten miles long, was sandy, and the water was permeable, and the soil did not stick together. There were twenty or thirty holes. Wang Gongyu, Liu Xinyuan, Zhang Yaxuan, and other technical personnel led the civilians to rush to block the holes all night, wading into the water barefoot, using people to block the flow, and putting down linen bags of soil. However, because this place is where the microcurrent directly exits south, the water force is too strong, and it is difficult to close the gap. The supervising personnel and working civilians have not slept for three days and nights.

Open-Air Meeting on the Dike 78

Wang Gongyu invited the Party and government personnel to inspect the dike, and immediately convened an open-air meeting on the dike. The consensus was that it was difficult to determine whether the first water defense line could be blocked in the future, and preparations should be made for the second water defense line. A large dike was proposed to be built from Pipa Mountain to Jinpu Road. In the event that Lanjia Dam and the western dike could not be held, the Jing River and Bulao River would overflow greatly, and this would be used as a defense. However, the first water defense line should still be blocked with all efforts. However, the civilians are working extremely hard, with some suffering from diseases due to the scorching sun, others injuring their limbs by splitting stones, and still others going hungry because no one has the strength to deliver food. It was proposed that the Party and government leaders return to the city to send representatives to the province to request a large sum of money for relief to facilitate the blockage. Everyone returned to the city in the evening.

Special Commissioners Personally Inspect 79

After Special Commissioner Shao Hanyuan received urgent information from northern Tongshan yesterday, he immediately added Wang Picheng, Chief of Staff of the Security Command, and Zhao Yuxin, Director of the Public Security Bureau, who rushed to assist County Magistrate Wang in supervising the construction and blockage in the afternoon. The county government secretary, Jian Hua, was ordered to requisition linen bags, seal the vehicles, and transport materials to the dangerous places overnight to provide assistance. After the Party and government personnel returned to the city to report to Shao, Shao believed that if the first water defense line was abandoned, Tongshan would be sacrificed too much. It should still be blocked desperately and not withdrawn until the last resort. Therefore, this morning he personally rushed to inspect, determined to block and prepare for subsequent defense plans. According to his statement, the original plan for preventing the Yellow River in this area was not to block the water from flowing down, so dams were built and dikes were repaired, leaving out the Lanjia Dam mouth. When the Shandong representative came to Xuzhou to inspect, his opinion was respected, and the mouth was

Zhenru Institute of Forensic Medicine: Autopsies on the Corpses of Prison Inmates; Families May Claim the Bodies; Unclaimed Bodies Sent for Autopsy

Prison inmates of the Public Concession's Tilanqiao Prison who die from illness have traditionally had their corpses transported by the prison to the Forensic Examination Office on Avenue Petain. The First Special District Court's Procuratorate is then notified to dispatch a prosecutor and forensic medical examiners to the office. After verifying the cause of death, if the deceased has family, they are instructed to claim the body for burial. If unclaimed, the body is handed over to the Pushan Benevolent Association for burial. Recently, the Zhenru Institute of Forensic Medicine consulted with the First Special District, proposing to borrow the aforementioned unclaimed bodies for dissection and research to determine the causes of death from disease, thereby increasing medical knowledge. This request has been approved by the court. Therefore, yesterday morning, the corpses of three inmates – Ding Changming, 54 years old; Dan Debiao, 26 years old; and Chen Yongzhong, 28 years old – were still transported by the prison to the Forensic Examination Office. Prosecutor Song Genshan, dispatched by the First Special District Court, along with forensic medical examiner Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the office. They verified that all three bodies had died from illness and that no family members had come to claim them. Consequently, they instructed that the bodies of inmates Ding Changming, Dan Debiao, and Chen Yongzhong, who died from illness and had no family, be allowed to be dissected by the Institute of Forensic Medicine for research purposes. After the dissection, the bodies were to be handed over to the Pushan Benevolent Association for burial.

Along the Railway Lines: Discovery of Rare Antiquities, Mostly Found by Chance

Antiquities and historical sites possess invaluable research value for culture and scholarship. In recent years, China's academic circles have dedicated themselves to excavation, resulting in numerous discoveries. Recently, various locations along the Jinghu (Beijing-Shanghai), Huhang (Shanghai-Hangzhou), and Hangyong (Hangzhou-Ningbo) railways have also yielded successive discoveries, mostly found by chance. These finds provide valuable references for archaeologists. Excerpts are listed below:

Ancient Tomb

At the Liu Family Garden outside the Zhonghua Gate in Nanjing, the construction of the Jingwu (Nanjing-Wuhu) Railway's main station led to the excavation of an ancient tomb dating back 500 years. The tomb was constructed of massive stones, standing five feet high and resembling a stone house. Inside the tomb was a stone tablet, revealing that it was the burial site of Wang Yanying, a wealthy merchant from Wuxi, and his wife. The tomb was built on the twelfth day of the twelfth month of the forty-seventh year of the Wanli reign (Ming Dynasty).

Golden Cups

While working in the mulberry fields outside the East Gate of Wuxi at Tangjiaqiao, farmer Guo Fulin unearthed twelve golden wine cups. Each cup was stamped with a branding iron mark and weighed eight taels. He also found a golden water ladle weighing seven taels, totaling one hundred and three taels of gold. However, the dynasty to which these relics belong remains to be verified.

Ancient Well

An ancient well was recently discovered in the Qijiadun area of Songjiang. The well is filled with clear water and is estimated to be a relic from the Ming Dynasty, as General Qi Jiguang once stationed troops here to defend against the Japanese pirates.

Large Cauldron

At Wen Shi Jing (Well) of Jingjue Temple outside the Zhongshan Gate in Nanjing, a large bronze cauldron was discovered. It is engraved with landscapes, figures, flowers, birds, insects, fish, and other patterns, as well as inscriptions by Zhu Huchen from the Ming Dynasty.

Jade Bowls

Near the Guandi Temple on Tangshan Ridge in the border area between Hangzhou and Yuyao counties, workers were hired to excavate the site for building the Dizang Temple. During the excavation, a pair of ancient jade bowls was unearthed. The bowls are white, with a diameter of about thirteen centimeters. The dynasty to which these relics belong is yet to be determined.

City Center Railway Section Fully Completed; Awaiting Trial Run

In order to promote the prosperity of the city center and facilitate transportation, the Shanghai Municipal Government has collaborated with the Ministry of Railways to build a branch line from Songhu Road to the city center. The Municipal Government is responsible for requisitioning and providing private land, while the Ministry of Railways is responsible for materials. Since the commencement of construction by the two railway bureaus, the project has progressed rapidly. According to Wu Xijun, the director of the Document Section of the bureau, speaking to a reporter from the Huadong News Agency, the entire project has now been completed. The railway line starts near the 6.05-kilometer mark of the Jiangwan Station and extends directly to Sanmin Road, not far from the venue of the Sixth National Games. It involved the filling of four thousand two hundred cubic feet of earth and the construction of two wooden bridges, a station building, and a platform. The earthwork and wooden bridge projects were contracted to Changji and Cailinji construction companies respectively. All track-laying and other works have been completed, and the entire line is ready for traffic. It is now awaiting instructions from the bureau chief before a trial run can be conducted. The date of the official opening for passenger service and ticket sales is yet to be determined. Since there will be fewer people traveling to the city center before the opening of the National Games, an early opening might result in financial losses. Therefore, the official opening for passenger service and ticket sales is expected to be on October 1st, as the National Games will open on October 10th.

Severe Dysentery Outbreak on Rue Shiga: Transmitted by Dung Beetles, Especially Affecting Children

According to yesterday's Japanese newspaper, the Shanghai Japanese Daily, a severe dysentery outbreak has recently occurred in the Liuqing Xiaozhu area on Rue Shiga. Among families of Chinese, Westerners, and Japanese, several children between the ages of four and nine have died within a dozen days. Although these families are of different nationalities and unrelated, their children often gather to play together, and the maids employed by each household frequently enter and exit through the back doors, leading to transmission from neighbor to neighbor. On the 23rd, Mr. Tsuneo Yoshioka conducted an investigation and research, tracing the transmission route. He has now determined that the vector is the oil worm (i.e., dung beetle), followed by indirect transmission through flies and fleas. Dr. Tsuboi of the Shinozaki Hospital has reached the same conclusion in his research. Young children are particularly susceptible to the disease. It is reported that those suffering from acute symptoms die within twelve hours. The bacteria are transmitted from dung beetles to food, and then enter the intestines through the stomach, spreading throughout the body. Once they invade the brain or heart, sudden and violent convulsions occur, or the patient develops typhoid fever, cholera, or dysentery, making it extremely dangerous. Currently, Japanese residents are working hard to eliminate oil worms and are undergoing preventive vaccinations.

Minghua Bank's Qian Zhen Case Adjudicated: Tong Jinhui and Others Found Not Guilty

The responsible persons of the now-defunct Minghua Bank, including the general manager, deputy general manager, and assistant manager, were successively sued by various creditors in the First Special District Court for fraud and breach of trust. Several such cases exist. After the court summoned them for questioning, it ordered the suspension of proceedings in some of the cases, instructing the parties to apply to the Civil Court for liquidation according to the law. In cases where such an order was not issued, such as the case where Qian Zhen sued Minghua Chairman Tong Jinhui, General Manager Zhang Gangbo, Deputy Manager Yu Dehua, and Assistant Manager Miao Zhen for fraud, Judge Wu Zehan continued the hearing yesterday afternoon. Only Yu and Miao, along with their defense lawyers, appeared in court. Tong Jinhui, originally from Ningbo, was reportedly involved in a money shop in his hometown. Due to the recent financial turmoil in Ningbo, many money shops have closed or suspended operations, and Tong's shop has also been caught in the vortex. Upon hearing the news in Shanghai, Tong left for Ningbo a few days ago. His lawyer explained the situation, stating that Tong had said he would return to Shanghai for the hearing, but his absence suggested that special circumstances in Ningbo had prevented his travel. Next, Miao Zhen's lawyer stated that Minghua Bank had begun liquidation, with the Ministry of Finance sending personnel to supervise the process, as announced in the newspapers. Creditors should register their claims for liquidation. Defendant Yu Dehua stated that the plaintiff had voluntarily deposited the funds and was not induced by fraud. He counter-sued the plaintiff for false accusation. Miao Zhen stated that the problems in Shanghai were not due to local turmoil, but solely affected by the Qingdao branch. The fraud accusation was unexpected. As the facts were clear, the court proceeded to debate. The plaintiff's lawyer requested that the defendants be punished for their crimes and ordered to repay the plaintiff's deposit of 300 yuan and interest. After the defendants' lawyers presented their arguments, Judge Wu announced the verdict: Tong, Yu, and Miao were found not guilty, and Qian was also found not guilty. Qian's civil suit was dismissed. The charges against Zhang Gangbo will be reviewed when Zhang is apprehended.

A Child Scalded to Death in Hot Water: Clothing Stall Apprentice Accidentally Placed a Bucket of Hot Water, Unintentionally Causing the Death of a Child

Ding Baoqing, 50 years old, from Zhenjiang, is a tea attendant on the Taikoo Company's North River route Tongzhou steamer. His wife, Ding Wangshi, 36 years old, and their son, Shun'gen, 6 years old, reside in a room behind the parlor at Lane 4, Yuan Shang Street on Ningbo Road in the French Concession. On the evening of the 22nd of this month, a neighbor gave a pot of leftover hot water to Xu Chenshi (a 40-year-old widow), the landlady of the second house in Lane 4, for bathing. Chenshi, being busy, asked Bao Lin (a 14-year-old apprentice from Jiangbei at the Deshengji clothing stall in the parlor) to fetch the water. She instructed Bao Lin to pour the water into a washbasin. However, Bao Lin mistakenly poured the water into a foot-bathing bucket and placed the bucket in the passageway, awaiting landlady Xu Chenshi to use it for washing. He loudly informed everyone in the residence that there was a bucket of hot water in the passageway, blocking the way, and asked them to use the back door. Ding Wangshi was in the room at the time, and her son, Shun'gen, was playing outside the main door, enjoying the cool air. After drinking tea inside, Shun'gen wanted to go to the back door. The child was unaware of the hot water bucket in the passageway and walked straight ahead, tripping over the bucket. He fell into the hot water, and his hands, arms, and chest were scalded by the boiling water, causing redness, swelling, and peeling skin. Upon hearing the sound, his mother rushed out and pulled the child out. Initially, the child was in extreme pain and unable to speak. After being revived, old insect oil was applied for first aid before being rushed to Guangren Hospital for treatment, which proved ineffective. The child died at the hospital at 4:20 PM the next day. Upon hearing the news, the child's mother confronted the landlady, Qian Chenshi, and beat the clothing apprentice, Bao Lin, causing a head injury. Bao Lin reported the incident to the French Concession Police, who sent detectives to investigate. Initially, Ding Wangshi wanted the landlady to pay for the expenses, but the landlady refused, claiming that the child scalded himself to death. The police transported the child's body to the Tongren Fuyuan Mortuary. Yesterday, they reported to the Second Special District Court, and Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with a forensic medical examiner and clerk, arrived at the mortuary at noon to examine the body. After hearing the report from the detectives and questioning the child's mother, Ding Wangshi, the landlady, Qian Chenshi, and the clothing apprentice, Bao Lin, the official concluded that Ding Shun'gen had indeed died from being scalded by hot water during his lifetime. The body was handed over to the child's mother for burial after she signed a guarantee. However, the child's mother had no funds. As a result, a neighbor with the surname of Mou provided funds to purchase a coffin for burial.

Meilong Station Master Cai Lianqing Killed by Train: Strong Wind Blamed

The No. 1 Beijing-Zhabei express train arrived at the North Shanghai Station at 2:30 PM yesterday and departed at 3:15 PM. As the train passed Meilong Station at approximately 3:50 PM, Station Master Cai Lianqing, as usual, went to the platform to signal the train through with a flag. Unfortunately, due to a strong gust of wind, he was suddenly struck by the train and thrown onto the tracks. His head, abdomen, and even limbs were severed, and his internal organs spilled out, a gruesome sight. He died instantly. As the station is small, with only Station Master Cai overseeing all affairs, including ticket sales and telegrams, along with a porter and a railway policeman, the accident could not be reported immediately. It was not until the Beijing-Zhabei express train arrived at Xin Zhuang Station that the conductor reported the incident to Station Master Zhu Moutong, who immediately telegraphed both the Traffic and Locomotive Departments, as well as Zhong Wenjiang, the section chief of the South Station Traffic Section. Zhong immediately led Lu Jiazhen, the relief station master from the South Station, and Zhu Jianben (the station master's son-in-law), a baggage handler, to Meilong Station on the 7.05 Shanghai-Jiading local train at 4:20 PM to manage all station affairs and investigate the details of the accident. Zhong assigned Lu Jiazhen, the relief station master, to temporarily assume the duties of Meilong Station Master. It is understood that Cai Lianqing, the Meilong Station Master, was 51 years old and from Haining, Zhejiang. He had been serving the railway since February of the ninth year before the founding of the Republic (1903), totaling 33 years of dedicated service. Known for his loyalty and kindness, he was promoted to station master and earned a monthly salary of over one hundred yuan. He left behind four sons and one daughter. His wife had passed away eight years ago. The eldest daughter is married to Zhu Jianben, a baggage handler at the South Station. The two eldest sons are still in school, and the third and fourth sons are in elementary school, raised by their elder sister. Cai himself lived alone at the station, and his situation can be described as lonely. His death in the line of duty has sparked various rumors. Some say his physical condition might have led to his eventual retirement. In addition to the existing pension of approximately three thousand yuan, the Railway Bureau intends to provide generous compensation in recognition of his long service, diligence, and tragic death in the line of duty.

American Zoologist Mr. Dolan Completes Expedition to Tibet and Returns to Shanghai: A Year of Hardship Yields a Rich Collection of Strange Animals; To Return to the United States Soon

Mr. Brooke Dolan, a renowned young American zoologist and explorer, recently returned to Shanghai after an expedition to Tibet in China. He arrived a few days ago, bringing with him many previously unseen strange beasts. Dolan previously worked at the Nanjing Central Museum of Natural History. He departed Shanghai on July 3 last year, passing through Chongqing, Sichuan, and over Dartsemdo (Kangding). He was accompanied by a team of Tibetan locals. In January of this year, he safely arrived at Tanggula Pass on the border of Qinghai, an important gateway to Tibet. He faced some difficulties there due to obstruction from Muslims, but Dolan's hard work eventually secured permission from the local government, allowing him to reach his destination and carry out his work. He collected many animals, such as the yak and antelope. Dolan's expedition to Tibet took him through areas mostly over 14,000 feet above sea level, including a 150-mile stretch almost entirely uninhabited. This arduous journey lasted thirty to forty days, and Dolan's courageous spirit led to considerable success. Dolan is expected to return to the United States from Shanghai soon.

The North China Daily News reported that American explorer Dolan quietly returned to Shanghai two months ago, laden with animal specimens collected from the Chinese interior. He has been residing quietly in a hotel. A reporter met with him yesterday to discuss the expedition. Dolan previously participated in an expedition in 1931 for the Philadelphia Academy of Natural Sciences to collect materials on the giant panda and other animals. This recent expedition was also commissioned by the Philadelphia Academy of Natural Sciences and supported by the Nanjing Central Academic Research Institute. Dolan's second expedition departed Shanghai in the winter of 1934, accompanied by Dr. Schäfer, a zoologist from the University of Göttingen in Germany, and Mr. Duncan, who had been a missionary in Batang for ten years. Their goal was to penetrate regions previously unvisited by foreign biologists, including several hundred square miles of eastern Tibet, ranging from 9,000 to 17,000 feet above sea level. They also hoped to observe the Anyemaqen Mountains. The specific aim of the expedition was to locate habitats of wild yaks, McNair's deer, and Tibetan brown bears for the Philadelphia Academy of Natural Sciences and to film wildlife in the Tibetan highlands. In June 1934, Dolan and his team of three, along with fifteen Tibetans, set off from Dartsemdo with fifty yaks to carry their luggage. They planned to hunt in the high slopes near the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and in Litangba during the autumn and early winter, establishing their winter base in Batang. They obtained several valuable wild animal specimens there. The team later traveled from Batang to Qinghai. En route, they detoured north for seven days due to banditry, passing through sparsely populated areas and finding themselves in the highest regions of eastern Tibet. In mid-March, they reached the border of Qinghai and obtained several specimens of McNair's deer, the most valuable of their collection. While the specimens may not appear extraordinary, the scientific community only knew of two females obtained by Captain McNair in 1900. This animal never breeds at altitudes below 19,400 feet. They also obtained several specimens of the Tibetan wild ass. The team originally planned to form another group to travel to Xining and collect wild yaks, Tibetan long-horned antelopes, and large bears along the way. However, border officials would not allow them to enter their territory, whether westward or northward. Consequently, on April 15, Dolan led two Tibetans and three pack animals across the upper reaches of the Yellow River, detouring 500 miles to reach Xining. They requested permission from the Qinghai provincial authorities to penetrate the origins of the Wen River and the upper reaches of the Yangtze River to find highland wildlife. The upper reaches of the Yellow River are full of marshy quicksand, an endless expanse with no smoke and difficult for travelers to traverse. Lacking landmarks, they had to rely on a compass, making it extremely dangerous, as the area is rife with bandits who specialize in robbery and murder. Dolan once got lost in the wilderness for nine days, surviving solely on wild ass meat, with ass dung as fuel. Fortunately, he encountered a caravan that guided him back to the correct path, allowing him to reach Xining safely. Dolan rested in Xining for a few days before proceeding to Lanzhou, where he took a plane to Shanghai. His wife had been anxiously waiting for his return. The journey from the Qinghai border to Xining taken by Dolan has not been attempted by foreigners since General Prejevalsky, the famous British military explorer, passed through the area. Duncan and Schäfer are currently seeking a route to Chongqing with their collection of bird and animal specimens from eastern Tibet before returning to Shanghai. The completeness of their collection is unprecedented.

West Lake Condensed Milk Company Launches Swallow Brand Milk Powder: Glorious Crystallization of National Goods

Currently, the milk powder sold in the market is mostly from foreign countries, resulting in a substantial outflow of funds every year, which is alarming. In view of this situation, the Hangzhou West Lake Condensed Milk Company has invented and manufactured a national product, "Swallow Brand Milk Powder." After repeated laboratory tests, it has been declared a success. This is truly a glorious achievement for national goods this year.

Company's Founding

The company was founded in 1927 by Su Jia'gan, Zhang Xiongfei, and others, originally named "Hangzhou Disinfected Milk Company." As its business grew, it was renamed "West Lake Condensed Milk Company." It specializes in the production of disinfected fresh milk, condensed milk, butter, fresh cream, and other products, all of which are exquisite and renowned far and wide.

Efficacy No Different from Breast Milk

Now, sparing no effort, it has produced "Swallow Brand Milk Powder." After a year of research and laboratory testing, using scientific methods, this milk powder is rich in vitamins. Its elements are no different from breast milk, making it the best breast milk substitute for infants, superior to imported products.

A Glimpse of the Complete Scale

The company owns thousands of acres of pasture, with the first, second, and third pastures located in Wengjiabu and Yuhang. It raises over 400 world-renowned New Zealand dairy cows. Specialized personnel are hired to oversee feeding and milking. The area is located near the Tianmu Mountains, with beautiful scenery and excellent air quality, making it ideal for natural forage and drinking water for the cows. Therefore, the milk produced is particularly good.

Sales to Begin Soon

At the same time, the company's equipment is quite complete. The disinfection rooms and cold storage rooms are equipped with excellent machinery. Great attention is paid to hygiene in the manufacturing, canning, and packaging processes. After fresh milk is taken from the pasture, it is transported to the factory in company vehicles, where it is disinfected before being processed into condensed milk or milk powder. The process is clean, fast, and unparalleled. It is reported that this "Swallow Brand Milk Powder" will soon be launched in Shanghai and other cities nationwide.

As the hot summer is ending and cool autumn is approaching, the disaster victims without clothes and food urgently need donations from all sectors to be rescued. All staff members are volunteers, and all performances are also volunteer performances. The ticket proceeds are managed by accountants Pan Xulun, Xi Yushu, and Xu Xiaochu. Commercial News & Finance: Foreign Banks Suddenly Rise; Standard Gold Price Further Drops by 3.6 Yuan; Exchange Market Gradually Tightens After Loosening, Falling and Rising Again; Closed for One Day on Confucius' Birthday, Tuesday

Gold Market 80

The gold market was weak yesterday due to a sudden surge in overseas silver markets. The exchange market initially loosened but then tightened, managing to recover. The Hong Kong market was erratic. As a result, the market situation fluctuated for most of the half-day. In the morning, overseas silver markets in both England and America rose in unison. The price of silver for forward delivery in Monterrey also rose by 0.013 to 0.0123, etc. Exchange rates slightly contracted. The price of raw gold in London rose by 1.5 pence. Unofficial forward trading opened, immediately falling to 712 yuan. Wing Lee, Wai Cheung, Tai Tat, Chun Yuen, and Wing Chun all took advantage of the low price to advance, pulling it up to 745 yuan. After the Central Bank's official rates were announced, both English and American currencies rose. The Customs Gold Unit fell by 0.09, and the standard gold price was lowered to 924.3 yuan, yet remained stable. Banks seized the opportunity to buy at low prices, stimulating buying and driving the price up. It was known in advance that HSBC's official exchange rate for English currency would rise by 0.125 and for American currency by 0.25. At this point, Chinese merchants bought American and sold English currency, fluctuating for some time. Later, Sassoon continued to buy shillings, tightening the exchange market and boosting confidence, pushing through the 80 yuan mark. Banks made some purchases, stabilizing the situation. However, because the Hong Kong market initially loosened and then tightened, the market situation appeared uncertain, hovering around 80 yuan for quite some time. Later, the Hong Kong market hardened again, and Chase Manhattan sold U.S. dollars, loosening the exchange market and causing it to fall back down, becoming soft for a time. British Defence Committee Given Power to Act Expediently 81

(London) The members of the Imperial Defence Committee, Lord Privy Seal MacDonald, Foreign Secretary Hoare, First Lord of the Admiralty Monsell, and Secretary of State for War Hore-Belisha, met today at Number 10 Downing Street to discuss the British Empire's naval, land, and air defenses. It is now known that the Cabinet has empowered the committee with the authority to act expediently. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(London) The Cabinet discussed yesterday the policy to deal with the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. However, it was decided to let the French government conduct negotiations with Italy, hoping to establish a compromise plan before the League of Nations Council meets. Regarding this matter, well-informed sources still have little hope, believing that what is being done now is to present the old suggestions to Italy again, that is, to redistribute the spheres of influence of Britain, France, and Italy in Abyssinia, and for Italy to obtain economic benefits that are even greater than those contained in the 1906 Tripartite Agreement. Italy once rejected this. In short, if this negotiation fails again, the Executive Council will decide to meet on September 4. At that time, delaying tactics may be adopted, such as appointing a committee to go to Africa to investigate the dispute on the spot and submit a report to the Executive Council, so that the war can be delayed, and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini can reconsider the possibility of a peaceful resolution. Italy can also send representatives to participate in the Executive Council meeting in September. However, if the war finally breaks out and cannot be stopped, the British government is determined to...at that time, it will not hesitate to impose sanctions on Italy. During yesterday's Cabinet meeting, the ministers studied the deployment of British naval, land, and air forces in the Mediterranean, the Near East, and near Africa, as well as the deployment of Italian forces in the same area. It can be seen that the British government, after the final failure of mediation efforts, will definitely demand the implementation of the League of Nations Covenant as a means of responding. (Havas Dispatch, 23rd)

(London) Britain today is determined to prevent Mussolini's colonial ambitions from endangering world peace and is planning various response measures to protect the Empire in case peaceful efforts fail. Currently, British diplomatic circles are still seeking a final diplomatic solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute and are taking joint action with France. The British Imperial Defence Committee met at Number 10 Downing Street. It is estimated that ten cabinet members discussed the preparations for the army, navy, and air force for twenty hours and twenty minutes. Another report states that Britain has issued a serious warning to Italy, but this has been denied by the authorities. (National News Agency Telegram, 23rd)

Italian-Abyssinian Arbitration Committee Met Yesterday in the Swiss Capital; Former Italian Governor Presented Testimony 82

Swiss Capital The Italian-Abyssinian Mixed Arbitration Committee held a meeting here at the Hotel Metropole this morning at 10:00 AM and listened to the testimony of the last of the witnesses summoned by the Italian representative regarding the Walwal incident. The main point of this testimony was to explain in detail the activities of the Italian army stationed in Abyssinia during the Walwal incident, as well as the incidents that occurred afterward between the Italian territory and the Abyssinian border. After the Arbitration Committee adjourned this morning, no communique was issued. The next meeting is scheduled for tomorrow. It is heard that the committee will leave here on Sunday. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

Swiss Capital The Italian-Abyssinian Conciliation Committee met at the Lakeside Hotel here yesterday, with strict security. The former Italian Governor of Somalia, Rella Vaffe, was the first to testify before the committee. Two East Africans who served in the Italian army during the Walwal incident have also arrived here to prepare to testify. (National Telegram, 24th)

Milan Commander Schermerle of the Italian army at Walwal set off today for the Swiss capital to testify before the Italian-Abyssinian Conciliation Committee regarding the Walwal incident. (National Telegram, 24th)

Swiss Capital Last night, a public demonstration against Fascism and the Italian-Abyssinian dispute took place. Two foreigners were preparing to give speeches to the crowd. One was a black man. The Swiss authorities dispersed them based on the August 30 order prohibiting all gatherings to avoid disrupting Switzerland's neutrality. (National Telegram, 24th)

Brenner Pass Italian Army Conducts Large-Scale Maneuvers 500,000 Troops Have Set Out 83

(Rome) 500,000 soldiers set out for the Brenner Pass today to conduct large-scale maneuvers, a rare occurrence since the European War. These maneuvers are intended to test the speed of movement and defensive strength of the troops at the foot of the Alps. The mock war will begin near the Austrian border, 30 miles from southern Germany, going back and forth from the air, 80 miles from Munich. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(Rome) The army is scheduled to begin large-scale maneuvers tomorrow in the areas of Bolzano, Udine, and Bergamo. More than 500,000 soldiers will participate, including the Alpine motorized units. The theme of the maneuvers is how to defend the country at the border between Italy and Austria in the event of war. Four of Italy's most famous generals are currently studying the situation in all aspects after the outbreak of war as a precaution. Major military and political figures in the capital and members of the royal family have all set out for the maneuver site. It is heard that King Victor Emmanuel III will personally observe the maneuvers. (Havas Dispatch, 23rd)

Germany Issues Public Bonds 84

In order to implement his plan to reorganize Germany's short-term debt, Economic Minister Schacht today issued government bonds with a 4.5% interest rate of 500 million Marks, with an actual receipt of 98.25. At the same time, the national bank issued treasury bills of 500 million Marks with a 4.5% interest rate, with an actual receipt of 98.75 and a term of ten years. (National Telegram, 24th)

(Berlin) According to today's news, the German government, in order to carry out its projects, is now planning to issue public bonds of 500 million Marks in the first half of September, with an actual receipt of 98.75 per hundred, an annual interest rate of 4%, and full repayment after ten years. Starting in 1941, 20% of the issued amount will be repaid each year. Another 500 million Marks of public bonds will be purchased entirely by savings banks. This move is roughly part of the plan to reduce the state's economic burden, as previously foreshadowed by Dr. Schacht, President of the Deutsche Bank and Acting Minister of Social Affairs. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

Page 10

US Agricultural Adjustment Administration Director Defends Cotton Loans Banking Act Signed by President 85

(Washington) Agricultural Adjustment Administration Director Davis is now vigorously defending the government's announced cotton loans of nine cents per pound and the method of directly guaranteeing that contracting cotton farmers will eventually receive a cotton price of twelve and a half cents. After the announcement of this method, cotton market prices fell sharply. Davis claims that the government's policy not only allows southern cotton farmers to obtain the best cotton production income they have enjoyed for many years, but also seeks to expand export markets, because the prosperity of the cotton industry is closely related to exports. He expects that this season will have the first cotton production worth one billion dollars since 1929. Democratic Senator Barnes initiated a movement this morning, advocating that legislation should be immediately enacted to force the authorities to implement a twelve and a half cent cotton loan. At the same time, Peng Haide urged cotton farmers to hoard cotton, waiting for a price of twelve and a half cents or higher, saying that they would rather sell their cotton at a reasonable price than accept the government's gratuity. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

(New York) Cotton industry experts are praising the government's new cotton debt policy as a guarantee of the free market and a constructive action to rebuild the advantage of American cotton in the world market. (National News Agency Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) Senator Payne has submitted an amendment to the Senate today, aiming to force the government to implement a twelve and a half cent cotton loan. This amendment is scheduled to be considered tomorrow. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

(New York) According to cotton statistics for the week ending August 23, the new cotton that has been listed this season totals 378,000 bales, which is more than both last week and the same time last year. The cotton sent to factories this week totaled 224,000 bales, which is also more than last week and the same time last year. Exports this week totaled 149,000 bales, with no major changes compared to before. New York's cotton inventory is the same as last week, but much less than the same time last year. The cotton inventory in American ports and inland towns this week is 2,214,000 bales, slightly more than last week, but also much less than the same time last year. The world's visible supply totals 4,373,000 bales, slightly less than last week, but much less than the same time last year. Since August 1 of this year, the American cotton used by factories around the world totals 515,000 bales, 160,000 bales more than last week, but slightly less than the same time last year. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) The amended Banking Act, finally passed by both houses of Congress, was signed and approved by President Roosevelt today. The government has thus obtained the power to control the loan policy of American banks. This act allows the government to guide the open market policy of the Federal Reserve Bank through a special committee composed of seven government representatives and five bank representatives. Furthermore, the President has the power to organize a new Federal Reserve Board before February 1, 1936, with the consent of the Senate. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) Democratic Senator McCarran declared today that he hoped the Senate would pass his proposal to abolish the 50% tax on silver profits, but admitted that the House of Representatives would not take any action on the bill before Congress adjourns this session. McCarran said he would ensure that the bill would be given priority in the Senate when Congress reconvenes early next year. Senator Thomas holds the same view. Congressman Martin and members of the House of Representatives' silver faction reiterated their previous statement to Associated Press reporters after consultations, stating that it is impossible to take action on this matter before Congress adjourns this session, but both houses of Congress are expected to take joint action when the next session of Congress convenes. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(London) Currency exchange experts claimed today that the US government is borrowing pounds sterling from the Bank of England to purchase silver in the London market, and that gold in New York is designated as collateral for this loan. The current state of the US dollar is sufficient to prove this statement. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) The House of Representatives today amended and passed the three-year rural mortgage plan proposed by Frazier-Lemke. This bill advocates that the government issue 300 million yuan in paper money to subsidize the financial needs of rural mortgages at low interest rates. This bill had previously been passed by the Senate, and now the House of Representatives has amended it. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) The House of Representatives today passed the mortgage moratorium bill proposed by Frank and Lemke. The bill allows farmers to apply for bankruptcy and recover their property within three years. It has now been sent to the White House for President Roosevelt to sign. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) Congress has the appearance of adjourning tonight, because the Senate and House of Representatives have reached a compromise on important issues that evening. (National News Agency Telegram, 24th)

Heavy Rain in Northern Japan Unprecedented in Fifty Years 52 People Dead 86

(Tokyo) Heavy rain has been falling frequently in the Tsugaru area of northern Japan, unprecedented in its intensity in fifty years. The flooded area is quite extensive, and hundreds of houses have been washed away by whirlpools. There have also been instances of landslides. According to official estimates, 12,000 houses have been damaged, and 20,000 acres of paddy fields and apple orchards are entirely under water. To date, 52 people have died, and 75 others have been injured. Several thousand people are homeless, and the loss is valued at a total of 10 million yen. Relief efforts are currently being expedited. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

Aomori Heavy rain continues to fall in the Tsugaru region, and the rivers are overflowing, with turbid water surrounding villages. Fire brigades and reservists have been mobilized to stand guard. If this situation continues, the villages will inevitably suffer a major disaster. (Japan Union Telegram, 24th)

Morioka The heavy rain in the Aomori region has caused a disaster. Rivers in Iwate and Akita prefectures have also overflowed, causing significant damage to crops. (Japan Union Telegram, 24th)

Dutch East Indies Government Restricts Japanese Entry to Prevent Unemployment Among Europeans 87

Batavia The Dutch East Indies government issued a regulation on the 23rd restricting the entry of foreign employees, which will be implemented from the 24th. The content of the regulation states that when Europeans and people from countries treated as Europeans, such as Japan, Iran, and Turkey, are employed by residents in the Dutch East Indies, they must obtain permission from the Attorney General. Therefore, with the exception of those who go to the Dutch East Indies alone to engage in business, those who seek employment cannot enter the country. The Dutch East Indies government declared that the purpose of the order is to prevent unemployment among Europeans, but its intention is nothing more than to restrict the entry of Japanese. Because Chinese people are not treated as Europeans, they are not subject to this restriction. (Japan Union Telegram, 24th)

Another Coal Mine Explosion in England Masked Rescuers Working in Shifts All Night 88

(London) Last night, a coal mine explosion occurred in South Elmsall, Yorkshire, killing several workers. This is the sixth major mine disaster in England this year. Masked rescuers worked in shifts all night, recovering two bodies. Fourteen people were injured, but five of them died this morning due to their injuries. One of the rescuers was trapped in the mine by gas. After four hours of searching, he was found unconscious. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

Political Upheaval in Yugoslavia Three Cabinet Members Resign 89

Belgrade Since Prime Minister Stojadinović formed the "Yugoslav Radical Union Party" by uniting with the former Serbian Radical Party, the Bosnian Muslim Party, and the Slovenian People's Party, and appointed himself leader, the former Serbian right-wing Democratic Party and the Croatian People's Party have decided to refuse to join. According to the Zhenli Bao newspaper, cabinet members belonging to these two parties, namely Minister of Social Affairs Prica of the Croatian People's Party, Minister of Justice Auer, and Minister of Forestry Stefanović of the Serbian right-wing Democratic Party, have all submitted their resignations. However, well-informed sources believe that the cabinet will not be reorganized immediately and will wait until after the political conference of the Little Entente countries meets in Bled, Yugoslavia, on August 29. (Havas Dispatch, 23rd)

Belgrade The cabinet upheaval that has been launched in the past few days has become increasingly serious today. Minister of Justice Auer, Minister of Forestry Stefanović, and Minister of Social Policy Prica have all submitted their resignations to Prime Minister Stojadinović. The Prime Minister has just returned from an audience with the Regent in Vilt. The official reason for this cabinet upheaval has not been announced, but it is said to be due to the refusal to allow the formation of a new political party. This will make the solution to the Croatian national question even more difficult. (National Telegram, 23rd)

Current Status of World Silver Circulation 90

(London) Both the import and export of British silver increased during the week of August 20. Exports totaled £1,450,000, of which £1,430,000 was shipped to the United States. Exports for the previous week were £768,000, of which £751,000 was shipped to the United States. Imports this week totaled £1,466,000, coming from Japan (£319,000), Soviet Russia (£390,000), Belgium (£260,000), Australia (£220,000), France (£20,000), New Zealand (£74,000), Hong Kong (£883,000), and India (£210,000). Imports for the previous week totaled £78,000. The net import surplus this week was £16,000. The net import surplus for the previous week was £13,000. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) During the week ending August 16, American silver imports totaled $4,734,000, coming from the United Kingdom ($1,892,000), Mexico ($1,522,000), Canada ($717,000), Peru ($425,000), Chile ($57,000), the Philippines ($2,000), Guatemala ($6,000), Honduras ($59,000), Germany ($3,000), and Newfoundland ($47,000). This number is much less than the import number for the previous week, decreasing by $9,871,000. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

Gansu-Shaanxi Judge Disciplined 91

(Nanjing) Xie Weian, a judicial official in Gansu-Shaanxi County, was found to have violated the law and neglected his duties. After being impeached by the Supervisory Committee and referred for punishment, the Central Disciplinary Committee has now decided to record a demerit against Xie. (Central News Agency Telegram, 24th)

Total Number of Registered Factories and Technicians 92

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industries has now released statistics on the number of approved and registered factories and industrial technicians, as follows: 309 technicians, 182 assistant technicians, and 560 factories. (Central News Agency Telegram, 24th)
